< text>
Vallarta is mostly an Hispanic market, however, there are plenty of products for everyone. The aisles are very small, and it's difficult to maneuver when there's another shopper in the aisle.
The "supermarket" has several self-chekout
Registers, which are very convenient.
In closing. I will say that Vallarta Market is a good little store, and I mostly shop there for sugar and coffee creamer, and frozen dinners. The supermarket is perfect for Hispanic community, and for basics such as sugar and coffee.</text>

Tightly packed Vallarta reminiscent of old-time grocery stores. The fresh food, prepared food, fruit and vegetables are all great and reasonably priced. Carries most all the Latin American brands and products so hard to find elsewhere. Friendly staff always helpful. Particularly fond of their own salsas (many), ensalada de pollo, zanahorias curtidas, rice pudding. Best place for Latin American tomatoes, tomatillos, peppers, cilantro and melons. Good chips and candy, too! Watch out crossing the street, though!<//review>

I couldn‚Äôt believe it...a $10 difference! I told them that it would have been nice if they would have mentioned when I dropped him off that it was only $10 more to get him groomed. Then I asked how much it would be for a hair cut without the bath and they said they don‚Äôt do that. So then I asked if the hardest part of grooming was the bath or the grooming, they said the grooming. Ok then...why a $10 difference? They couldn‚Äôt answer that question. Very disappointed in the service and the motive being to make as much money as they can on customers! I will not be bringing my dog here again. There‚Äôs too many reputable groomers available out there who both care about the customer and the animal!< /Text>

By far the best sushi I've had! I used to be local to this restaurant, but 5 yrs ago I moved out of state. I travel for work and have had sushi across our great states. No sushi has come close. Alex was our server at the time, and just as we finished our meal and were finishing up our wine, he walked over to us and asked us to leave. Apparently they had a reservation and needed the table, even though he sat us at the table to begin with and the party wasn't there. He didn't ask us if we could move, rather, he said "I hate to ask you to leave, but". His tone was incredibly rude, and I was immediately off put. Everyone was listening to him, and we felt like we were rushed, which was very embarrassing. He didn't apologize, and we left. The situation was made worse moments later. We got home, and called the restaurant asking to speak to a manager (his name was James). <user_id>109950024078908841344</user_id><username>Mar E</username>< date>
1563113479522<//date>
<rate>3<//rate><text>Boutique style restaurant. Popular with locals for its friendly staff. Wait times can be long due to its size & popularity. Four friends and I walked in an hour before closing and there was no wait. I think the crew was winding down after a long day of service & may not have been at the top of their game. Food service industry is a grueling master. We ordered both, family style plates, sushi & rolls to share. The place has some unique appetizers & specials/offerings of the day. On this particular evening, we tried an assortment of dishes. First up, chirashi, which included the standard fish (salmon, 2-types of tuna, yellow tail, octopus, shrimp, snapper, mackarel, uni) and the freshness of the fish was good, although the portion was small (it contained mostly rice) & could easily be a main for one person; however, not larger enough to share. Next, we tried the yakisoba, which was sizzling hot, large enough to share & have one portion left for lunch. It contained mostly veggies, some chicken, & the noodles we're firm and fork tender-which from my perspective is difficult to attain for some establishments. The flavor profile for this dish was standard & not to salty. Next up was the standard Tempura plate, a bit on the oily side & the batter was squishy, not crispy light & airy. The description sounded good but the deliverable was meh. The rolls we tried were mostly started with a California roll base and then topped off with your choice of fish. Again, standard, familiar types. The fish was fresh, good, but, for my taste (more adventurous), these rolls lacked the wow factor. For a local place, it's a bit more "up scale" (the price point reflects that), & maybe it was our timing (1 hr before closing) the food was ok. Will definitely try this place for an earlier dinner to see if the food flavors have a bit more omph in them. In the meantime, y'all go & try those independent gastronomies near you. Some are amazing & each is vying for you to have an awesome flavor experience. Itadakimasu.<//text><pics>None</pics><resp>None</resp><gmapID>0x80c326382c258819:0x12f651f0d2d9404< /gmapID></record>

< Review>
I've been to many other Hometown Buffet locations and I must say that this one is my least favorite location. First thing that caught my attention that I really disliked about this place is after I paid and walked past the kitchen area I could hear a lot of profanity and horse-playing going on in the back, which sounded very unprofessional - and not to mention there were alot of young children present whom I'm sure could hear the vulgar language coming from the back as well as I could. Secondly, the quality of food here was really not that great at all. The food was very tasteless and bland. I didn't even want to finish eating here because I just wasn't feeling the tasteless and half cooked food.

Not to sound too harsh here, but in all honesty if those guys in the kitchen put a little more pride in what they are cooking and put less time into goofing around and horse-playing and cussing at each other - the food might actually taste good here. As of right now, I will probably not return to this Hometown Buffet. I wouldn't recommend bringing your kids here either unless you want them hearing alot of profanity coming from the kitchen.<//Review>
